    Mar 17, 2011 01:13 PM UTC by OSG-GOC 
    Michael Ernst at WLCG daily meetinghttps://twiki.cern.ch/twiki/bin/view/LCG/WLCGDailyMeetingsWeek110110#Wednesday :
CNAF-BNL network problem (slow transfers) GGUS:61440 (since 2010-08-23)

* The last update on 2010-12-17: "News from NRNs side: It seems the "Production Path" has been cleared. A commissioning phase is ongoing." [ Michael - production link has been re-engineered - a new circuit has been setup. Tests initiated by ESNET engineering which look fine so far. They want to ramp-up traffic so that it looks like production to see if there is packet loss. Engineering still working, ESNET, USLHCNET and GEANT involved. News in next days ]
* ATLAS can perform some test transfers once the "commissioning" is done and the sites request it.
-- by Maria Dimou-Zacharova at Thu Mar 17 13:11:24 UTC 2011
    Mar 16, 2011 12:19 PM UTC by OSG-GOC 
    Following the completion of the work performed by network engineering from
DANTE on the re-engineered circuit between Amsterdam and Vienna BNL personnel
has conducted transfer tests in both directions between BNL and CNAF. Transfers
in both directions were observed at a rate of >500 MB/s, which is 80% of the
available bandwidth (4 out of 5 Gbps). During the time the tests were conducted
no packet loss was observed.

We will leave the ticket open for one more month and close it once we can
confirm that there are no more transfer problems.

Michael Ernst

> > > > -- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 01 11:50:23 UTC 2010
> > > >
> > > > Hello.
> > > >
> > > > From Chris Tracy at ESNet, (note: It will extend to the next
> > entries
> > > > due to character limit.)
> > > >
> > > > -------------------------
> > > > I have just completed several tests with help from Azher Mughal
> in
> > > the
> > > > USLHCnet domain.
> > > >
> > > > I ran 30 second, 100Mbps UDP tests with bwctl between aofa-
> > > pt1.es.net
> > > > and ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Loss was seen in the NYC
> to
> > > > Vienna direction, but the reverse direction was clean in every
> > test.
> > > >
> > > > The path under test is:
> > > >
> > > > ESnet aofa-sdn1 -- USLHCnet E600 -- Ciena NYC -- Ciena AMS --
> > > E600AMS
> > > > --
> > > > SARA.nl -- GEANT in Amsterdam -- GEANT in Vienna
> > > >
> > > > This path primarily consists of Layer-2 Ethernet and SONET/SDH.
> It
> > > is
> > > > 10GigE from aofa-sdn1 to the Ciena NYC. On the Ciena, it is
> mapped
> > > > into
> > > > a STS-1-96v (5G) circuit across the Atlantic. Once it gets to
> AMS,
> > > it
> > > > is passed through the E600 and handed off to SARA as Ethernet.
> We
> > > > have
> > > > setup port mirroring on USLHCnet's E600 in AMS for the purpose
> of
> > > > counting packets. VLAN tag 2607 is used all the way from ESnet
> to
> > > > SARA.
> > > > I am not sure how the SARA--GEANT portion of the circuit is
> > handled,
> > > > but
> > > > I'm assuming it has been provisioned over an SDH circuit of
> > > comparable
> > > > capacity -- e.g., VC-4-32v?
> > > >
> > > > Here is a traceroute between ESnet's perf tester (aofa-
> pt1.es.net)
> > > and
> > > > GEANT's perf tester (ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net ):
> > > >
> > > > # traceroute ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net
> > > > traceroute to ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58),
> 64
> > > hops
> > > > max, 40 byte packets
> > > > 1 aofa-te-perf-if1 (198.124.238.41) 0.155 ms 0.102 ms 0.086 ms
> > > > 2 esnet.rt1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.125.93) 101.117 ms 101.127
> ms
> > > > 101.371 ms
> > > > 3 ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58) 101.163 ms
> > > > 101.397
> > > > ms 101.511 ms
> > > >
> > > > Azher and I both ran tcpdump to count packets and compared the
> > > numbers
> > > > to the bwctl output. I am going to primarily focus on the NYC ->
> > > > Vienna
> > > > direction, as I have not observed any loss with 100Mbps UDP
> tests
> > in
> > > > the
> > > > reverse direction.
> > > >
> > > > Here is the summary of 5 tests in the NYC -> Vienna direction,
> > > showing
> > > > between 0.2% and 0.48% loss each time:
> > > >
> > > > TEST 1: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375586470 Bytes 100156068 bits/sec
> > > > 0.021
> > > > ms 903/256404 (0.35%)
> > > > TEST 2: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 376156830 Bytes 100308699 bits/sec
> > > > 0.014
> > > > ms 506/256395 (0.2%)
> > > > TEST 3: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375074910 Bytes 100020313 bits/sec
> > > > 0.027
> > > > ms 1242/256395 (0.48%)
> > > > TEST 4: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375471810 Bytes 100125953 bits/sec
> > > > 0.020
> > > > ms 974/256397 (0.38%)
> > > > TEST 5: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375468870 Bytes 100125236 bits/sec
> > > > 0.020
> > > > ms 974/256395 (0.38%)
> > > >
> > > > During these tests, Azher and I wrote packet captures to disk.
> The
> > > > port
> > > > mirroring host in AMS is using a version of libpcap < v1.0.0, so
> > > > tcpdump
> > > > cannot set the buffer size with -B. As a result, the first
> couple
> > of
> > > > tests were inconclusive due to pcap buffers being exhausted.
> Once
> > > > Azher
> > > > lowered the snaplen parameter to tcpdump, our packet counts
> > started
> > > to
> > > > match up.
> > > >
> > > > Here are two detailed examples. TEST 5 was over UDP port 5004.
> > iperf
> > > > reported 974 packets lost out of 256395 total.
> > > >
> > > > On the ESnet test host, we captured a total of 256455 packets
> > going
> > > to
> > > > ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Filtering out only port 5004
> > gives
> > > > us
> > > > 256398. Notice there is a difference of 3 packets. This is
> because
> > > > the
> > > > very last packet was in the reverse direction, and iperf always
> > > seems
> > > > to
> > > > report 2 less than reality. (see output below)
> > > >
> > > > -------------------------------

> > > > Hello.
> > > >
> > > > From Joe Metzger:
> > > > -----
> > > > ESnet has seen a significant improvement in our test results
> > today.
> > > > Both
> > > > GEANT adding additional capacity on their path and Azher adding
> > the
> > > > shaping
> > > > on the Force 10 seems to have had an affect.
> > > >
> > > > We saw an order of magnitude drop in packet loss in UDP tests,
> and
> > > we
> > > > saw a
> > > > TCP test up in the 900Mbps range from NYC to VIE right after the
> > > > shaping was
> > > > deployed. Test performance seems to have dropped off a bit in
> the
> > > last
> > > > couple hours,
> > > > but we have also seen significant increases in the utilization
> of
> > > the
> > > > link which
> > > > might account for some of that effect.
> > > >
> > > > But at this point, I am questioning if the problem we are
> > > experiencing
> > > > is
> > > > some sort of fault in a piece of equipment that can be replaced
> > once
> > > > we
> > > > identify it, or if there are inherent problems in the design of
> > this
> > > > path
> > > > and the equipment implementing it that we didn't know about. The
> > > > changes
> > > > that are improving performance are pointing to an inherent
> > equipment
> > > > limitations.
> > > >
> > > > I think we should seriously consider taking this path out of
> > > service,
> > > > and then
> > > > rigorously testing it to see if it is capable of meeting the
> > typical
> > > > standards
> > > > that ESnet has for wide area links. (IE it should be able to
> > > transfer
> > > > 50 Terabytes
> > > > with less than 100 packets dropped.) If it is not capable of
> > > > performing at these
> > > > levels, then I would like to discover what components or
> sections
> > of
> > > > the path
> > > > are causing the problems and better characterize them so we can
> > > > develop
> > > > a plan
> > > > to fix them or work around them.
> > > >
> > > > Does anybody object to proceeding with this plan early next
> week?
> > > >

> > > >
> > > >

> > > > > -- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 01 11:50:23 UTC 2010
> > > > >
> > > > > Hello.
> > > > >
> > > > > From Chris Tracy at ESNet, (note: It will extend to the next
> > > entries
> > > > > due to character limit.)
> > > > >
> > > > > -------------------------
> > > > > I have just completed several tests with help from Azher
> Mughal
> > in
> > > > the
> > > > > USLHCnet domain.
> > > > >
> > > > > I ran 30 second, 100Mbps UDP tests with bwctl between aofa-
> > > > pt1.es.net
> > > > > and ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Loss was seen in the NYC
> > to
> > > > > Vienna direction, but the reverse direction was clean in every
> > > test.
> > > > >
> > > > > The path under test is:
> > > > >
> > > > > ESnet aofa-sdn1 -- USLHCnet E600 -- Ciena NYC -- Ciena AMS --
> > > > E600AMS
> > > > > --
> > > > > SARA.nl -- GEANT in Amsterdam -- GEANT in Vienna
> > > > >
> > > > > This path primarily consists of Layer-2 Ethernet and
> SONET/SDH.
> > It
> > > > is
> > > > > 10GigE from aofa-sdn1 to the Ciena NYC. On the Ciena, it is
> > mapped
> > > > > into
> > > > > a STS-1-96v (5G) circuit across the Atlantic. Once it gets to
> > AMS,
> > > > it
> > > > > is passed through the E600 and handed off to SARA as Ethernet.
> > We
> > > > > have
> > > > > setup port mirroring on USLHCnet's E600 in AMS for the purpose
> > of
> > > > > counting packets. VLAN tag 2607 is used all the way from ESnet
> > to
> > > > > SARA.
> > > > > I am not sure how the SARA--GEANT portion of the circuit is
> > > handled,
> > > > > but
> > > > > I'm assuming it has been provisioned over an SDH circuit of
> > > > comparable
> > > > > capacity -- e.g., VC-4-32v?
> > > > >
> > > > > Here is a traceroute between ESnet's perf tester (aofa-
> > pt1.es.net)
> > > > and
> > > > > GEANT's perf tester (ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net ):
> > > > >
> > > > > # traceroute ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net
> > > > > traceroute to ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58),
> > 64
> > > > hops
> > > > > max, 40 byte packets
> > > > > 1 aofa-te-perf-if1 (198.124.238.41) 0.155 ms 0.102 ms 0.086 ms
> > > > > 2 esnet.rt1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.125.93) 101.117 ms
> 101.127
> > ms
> > > > > 101.371 ms
> > > > > 3 ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58) 101.163 ms
> > > > > 101.397
> > > > > ms 101.511 ms
> > > > >
> > > > > Azher and I both ran tcpdump to count packets and compared the
> > > > numbers
> > > > > to the bwctl output. I am going to primarily focus on the NYC
> ->
> > > > > Vienna
> > > > > direction, as I have not observed any loss with 100Mbps UDP
> > tests
> > > in
> > > > > the
> > > > > reverse direction.
> > > > >
> > > > > Here is the summary of 5 tests in the NYC -> Vienna direction,
> > > > showing
> > > > > between 0.2% and 0.48% loss each time:
> > > > >
> > > > > TEST 1: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375586470 Bytes 100156068 bits/sec
> > > > > 0.021
> > > > > ms 903/256404 (0.35%)
> > > > > TEST 2: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 376156830 Bytes 100308699 bits/sec
> > > > > 0.014
> > > > > ms 506/256395 (0.2%)
> > > > > TEST 3: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375074910 Bytes 100020313 bits/sec
> > > > > 0.027
> > > > > ms 1242/256395 (0.48%)
> > > > > TEST 4: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375471810 Bytes 100125953 bits/sec
> > > > > 0.020
> > > > > ms 974/256397 (0.38%)

> > > > >
> > > > > During these tests, Azher and I wrote packet captures to disk.
> > The
> > > > > port
> > > > > mirroring host in AMS is using a version of libpcap < v1.0.0,
> so
> > > > > tcpdump
> > > > > cannot set the buffer size with -B. As a result, the first
> > couple
> > > of
> > > > > tests were inconclusive due to pcap buffers being exhausted.
> > Once
> > > > > Azher
> > > > > lowered the snaplen parameter to tcpdump, our packet counts
> > > started
> > > > to
> > > > > match up.
> > > > >
> > > > > Here are two detailed examples. TEST 5 was over UDP port 5004.
> > > iperf
> > > > > reported 974 packets lost out of 256395 total.
> > > > >
> > > > > On the ESnet test host, we captured a total of 256455 packets
> > > going
> > > > to
> > > > > ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Filtering out only port 5004
> > > gives
> > > > > us
> > > > > 256398. Notice there is a difference of 3 packets. This is
> > because
> > > > > the
> > > > > very last packet was in the reverse direction, and iperf
> always
> > > > seems
> > > > > to
> > > > > report 2 less than reality. (see output below)

> > > > > shaping was
> > > > > deployed. Test performance seems to have dropped off a bit in

> > > > last
> > > > > couple hours,

> > of
> > > > the
> > > > > link which

> > > > >
> > > > > But at this point, I am questioning if the problem we are
> > > > experiencing
> > > > > is
> > > > > some sort of fault in a piece of equipment that can be
> replaced
> > > once
> > > > > we
> > > > > identify it, or if there are inherent problems in the design
> of
> > > this
> > > > > path
> > > > > and the equipment implementing it that we didn't know about.
> The
> > > > > changes
> > > > > that are improving performance are pointing to an inherent
> > > equipment
> > > > > limitations.
> > > > >
> > > > > I think we should seriously consider taking this path out of
> > > > service,
> > > > > and then
> > > > > rigorously testing it to see if it is capable of meeting the
> > > typical
> > > > > standards
> > > > > that ESnet has for wide area links. (IE it should be able to
> > > > transfer
> > > > > 50 Terabytes
> > > > > with less than 100 packets dropped.) If it is not capable of
> > > > > performing at these
> > > > > levels, then I would like to discover what components or

> > > of

> > As to the situation my view is we have to spend some effort to
> assess
> > whether
> > the circuit is usable in production, either configured as a sub-rate
> > channel or
> > running at full OC-192 rate.
> >
> > Artur, ATLAS activities are not demanding until the end of the month
> > such that
> > you can go ahead and add b/w from BNL's primary circuits to the one
> to
> > be
> > tested, if that helps to get it to the full OC-192 rate without
> having
> > to cut
> > into your protection capacity. This change could be made as early as
> > today.
> >
> > Then I'd suggest carrying out tests in (at least) two steps
> > - Let Joe run his tests along the entire path, and provided the
> > results are
> > reasonable
> > - Re-route BNL/CNAF production traffic to use this circuit and
> monitor
> > its
> > behavior for a week before we finally decide whether we want to keep
> > the
> > circuit in production.
> >
> > Following the above we have to restore the full b/w on BNL's primary
> > circuits,
> > while we should keep the BNL/CNAF production traffic on the sub-rate
> > channel.
> > We will monitor its behavior and decide whether the quality is
> > acceptable. The
> > fact that our applications were observed to utilize >5 Gbps during
> > presumably
> > very short periods is not an argument not to use this channel. We
> > don't have to
> > provision for peak requirements. However, having said that, if the
> > channel
> > starts showing increased error/drop rates at 50% - 75% utilization
> it
> > may be
> > unusable.

> > > Tests are still running...
> > > -- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 01 11:50:23 UTC 2010
> > >
> > > Hello.
> > >
> > > From Chris Tracy at ESNet, (note: It will extend to the next
> entries
> > > due to character limit.)
> > >
> > > -------------------------
> > > I have just completed several tests with help from Azher Mughal in
> > the
> > > USLHCnet domain.
> > >
> > > I ran 30 second, 100Mbps UDP tests with bwctl between aofa-
> > pt1.es.net
> > > and ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Loss was seen in the NYC to
> > > Vienna direction, but the reverse direction was clean in every
> test.
> > >
> > > The path under test is:
> > >
> > > ESnet aofa-sdn1 -- USLHCnet E600 -- Ciena NYC -- Ciena AMS --
> > E600AMS
> > > --
> > > SARA.nl -- GEANT in Amsterdam -- GEANT in Vienna
> > >
> > > This path primarily consists of Layer-2 Ethernet and SONET/SDH. It
> > is
> > > 10GigE from aofa-sdn1 to the Ciena NYC. On the Ciena, it is mapped
> > > into
> > > a STS-1-96v (5G) circuit across the Atlantic. Once it gets to AMS,
> > it
> > > is passed through the E600 and handed off to SARA as Ethernet. We
> > > have
> > > setup port mirroring on USLHCnet's E600 in AMS for the purpose of
> > > counting packets. VLAN tag 2607 is used all the way from ESnet to
> > > SARA.
> > > I am not sure how the SARA--GEANT portion of the circuit is
> handled,
> > > but
> > > I'm assuming it has been provisioned over an SDH circuit of
> > comparable
> > > capacity -- e.g., VC-4-32v?
> > >
> > > Here is a traceroute between ESnet's perf tester (aofa-pt1.es.net)
> > and
> > > GEANT's perf tester (ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net ):
> > >
> > > # traceroute ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net
> > > traceroute to ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58), 64
> > hops
> > > max, 40 byte packets
> > > 1 aofa-te-perf-if1 (198.124.238.41) 0.155 ms 0.102 ms 0.086 ms
> > > 2 esnet.rt1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.125.93) 101.117 ms 101.127 ms
> > > 101.371 ms
> > > 3 ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58) 101.163 ms
> > > 101.397
> > > ms 101.511 ms
> > >
> > > Azher and I both ran tcpdump to count packets and compared the
> > numbers
> > > to the bwctl output. I am going to primarily focus on the NYC ->
> > > Vienna
> > > direction, as I have not observed any loss with 100Mbps UDP tests
> in
> > > the
> > > reverse direction.
> > >
> > > Here is the summary of 5 tests in the NYC -> Vienna direction,
> > showing
> > > between 0.2% and 0.48% loss each time:
> > >
> > > TEST 1: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375586470 Bytes 100156068 bits/sec
> > > 0.021
> > > ms 903/256404 (0.35%)
> > > TEST 2: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 376156830 Bytes 100308699 bits/sec
> > > 0.014
> > > ms 506/256395 (0.2%)
> > > TEST 3: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375074910 Bytes 100020313 bits/sec
> > > 0.027
> > > ms 1242/256395 (0.48%)
> > > TEST 4: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375471810 Bytes 100125953 bits/sec
> > > 0.020
> > > ms 974/256397 (0.38%)
> > > TEST 5: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375468870 Bytes 100125236 bits/sec
> > > 0.020
> > > ms 974/256395 (0.38%)
> > >
> > > During these tests, Azher and I wrote packet captures to disk. The
> > > port
> > > mirroring host in AMS is using a version of libpcap < v1.0.0, so
> > > tcpdump
> > > cannot set the buffer size with -B. As a result, the first couple
> of
> > > tests were inconclusive due to pcap buffers being exhausted. Once
> > > Azher
> > > lowered the snaplen parameter to tcpdump, our packet counts
> started
> > to
> > > match up.
> > >
> > > Here are two detailed examples. TEST 5 was over UDP port 5004.
> iperf
> > > reported 974 packets lost out of 256395 total.
> > >
> > > On the ESnet test host, we captured a total of 256455 packets
> going
> > to
> > > ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Filtering out only port 5004
> gives
> > > us
> > > 256398. Notice there is a difference of 3 packets. This is because
> > > the
> > > very last packet was in the reverse direction, and iperf always
> > seems
> > > to
> > > report 2 less than reality. (see output below)
> > >
> > > -------------------------------

> > > Hello.
> > >
> > > From Joe Metzger:
> > > -----
> > > ESnet has seen a significant improvement in our test results
> today.
> > > Both
> > > GEANT adding additional capacity on their path and Azher adding
> the
> > > shaping
> > > on the Force 10 seems to have had an affect.
> > >
> > > We saw an order of magnitude drop in packet loss in UDP tests, and
> > we
> > > saw a
> > > TCP test up in the 900Mbps range from NYC to VIE right after the
> > > shaping was
> > > deployed. Test performance seems to have dropped off a bit in the
> > last
> > > couple hours,
> > > but we have also seen significant increases in the utilization of
> > the
> > > link which
> > > might account for some of that effect.
> > >
> > > But at this point, I am questioning if the problem we are
> > experiencing
> > > is
> > > some sort of fault in a piece of equipment that can be replaced
> once
> > > we
> > > identify it, or if there are inherent problems in the design of
> this
> > > path
> > > and the equipment implementing it that we didn't know about. The
> > > changes
> > > that are improving performance are pointing to an inherent
> equipment
> > > limitations.
> > >
> > > I think we should seriously consider taking this path out of
> > service,
> > > and then
> > > rigorously testing it to see if it is capable of meeting the
> typical
> > > standards
> > > that ESnet has for wide area links. (IE it should be able to
> > transfer
> > > 50 Terabytes
> > > with less than 100 packets dropped.) If it is not capable of
> > > performing at these
> > > levels, then I would like to discover what components or sections
> of
> > > the path
> > > are causing the problems and better characterize them so we can
> > > develop
> > > a plan
> > > to fix them or work around them.
> > >
> > > Does anybody object to proceeding with this plan early next week?
> > >
> > > Graph showing link utilization jump after deploying shaping:
> > >
> > >

-- by hiroito at Thu Feb 24 16:19:38 UTC 2011
    Feb 17, 2011 12:58 PM UTC by OSG-GOC 
    Joe, Artur,
Thank you very much for the detailed update as to the progress and your
thoughts as to a possible path forward.

As to the situation my view is we have to spend some effort to assess whether
the circuit is usable in production, either configured as a sub-rate channel or
running at full OC-192 rate.

Artur, ATLAS activities are not demanding until the end of the month such that
you can go ahead and add b/w from BNL's primary circuits to the one to be
tested, if that helps to get it to the full OC-192 rate without having to cut
into your protection capacity. This change could be made as early as today.

Then I'd suggest carrying out tests in (at least) two steps
- Let Joe run his tests along the entire path, and provided the results are
reasonable
- Re-route BNL/CNAF production traffic to use this circuit and monitor its
behavior for a week before we finally decide whether we want to keep the
circuit in production.

Following the above we have to restore the full b/w on BNL's primary circuits,
while we should keep the BNL/CNAF production traffic on the sub-rate channel.
We will monitor its behavior and decide whether the quality is acceptable. The
fact that our applications were observed to utilize >5 Gbps during presumably
very short periods is not an argument not to use this channel. We don't have to
provision for peak requirements. However, having said that, if the channel
starts showing increased error/drop rates at 50% - 75% utilization it may be
unusable.

--
Michael

-----Original Message-----
From: Artur Barczyk [mailto:Artur.Barczyk@....]
Sent: Thursday, February 17, 2011 7:04 AM

    To: Joe Metzger
Cc: Ernst, Michael; Erik Oostveen; Harding Harding; Mughal Mughal; Sandor
Rozsa; Bigrow Bigrow; Xavier Martins-Rivas; Domenico Vicinanza; Nikolay
Manolov; NOC NOC; NEP; O' Connor, Michael P (ESNET); Zani Zani; Toby Rodwell;
Bill Johnston; Luca Rinaldi; operations; Girolamo De Girolamo; Engineering
Engineering; Marco Marletta; Harvey Newman; Hironori Ito
Subject: Re: [routing] Vienna DXC (1678MCC) Software Upgrade R4.2 to R4.5 |
Testing of Trans-Atlantic links | DANTE SDE ticket #11183

Hi Joe, Michael, All,

fully agree with Joe's opening. It's frustrating.
And to the possibility that this circuit, in its current state this will lead
to more headaches.

We know how the NYC-Vienna circuit behaves under test pattern traffic, so if
BNL&CNAF are agreeing, we should give it a try in constrained production mode.

However, are we even sure it's an effect of a sub-rate channel?
For all I know, we never did test such a connection at full rate, not to these
specs.

What I propose is to raise this channel's capacity temporarily to full OC-192,
and re-test.
As this will cut into our protection capacity, we can do this only for a
limited amount of time, say 1-2 weeks.
If GEANT can do the same, I would be in favour of doing it before we put
CNAF/BNL traffic on it, and test it to the 100TB specs.

It would be beneficial to all if we could move quickly with this, and conclude
rapidly on the usefulness of this channel.
As it is now, we've been wasting valuable resources for too long, which is my
main concern here.

If 10G should be clean, we'll need to include it in our (combined) capacity
planning.

Cheers,
Artur

On 02/17/2011 01:05 AM, Joe Metzger wrote:
> Michael,
> In a word, the current status is frustrating. The path is not up to
> the standards
> we typically expect. But after fixing several issues and analyzing
> all sorts of test results, I am slowly coming to the conclusion that
> it is probably as good as it will ever get with the current
> architecture and equipment.
>
> At this point there are some technical experts that say it is good
> enough and won't adversely impact the majority of users. Others are
> saying this level of loss is unacceptable, will cause difficult to
> diagnose problems, and should not be put into service.
>
> Before the LHCOPN meeting last week I was thinking about trying to
> work with the appropriate people at BNL & CNAF to measure performance
> before and after rolling this circuit back into production to get a
> quantitate measure of how it affects your use case.
>
> At last weeks meeting Stefano Zani said that CNAF has been
> successfully sustaining rates up to 8Gbps to BNL, and that going back
> to the path with a 5G bottleneck would be a problem.
>
> So, at this point I don't like any of my options. But I think the
> next move should probably be to go ahead and try go gather some
> quantitate measurements that allow us to compare the current path with the 5G
path.
>
>
> Does this sound reasonable to you? And should I work with Hiro on this?
>
>
> Longer term, I think we need to look at the options for eliminating
> the sub-rate portion of this circuit. But there are a bunch of issues
> that may make that a challenge.
>
>
>
> --Joe

> -- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 01 11:50:23 UTC 2010
>
> Hello.
>
> From Chris Tracy at ESNet, (note: It will extend to the next entries
> due to character limit.)
>
> -------------------------
> I have just completed several tests with help from Azher Mughal in the
> USLHCnet domain.
>
> I ran 30 second, 100Mbps UDP tests with bwctl between aofa-pt1.es.net
> and ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Loss was seen in the NYC to
> Vienna direction, but the reverse direction was clean in every test.
>
> The path under test is:
>
> ESnet aofa-sdn1 -- USLHCnet E600 -- Ciena NYC -- Ciena AMS -- E600AMS
> --
> SARA.nl -- GEANT in Amsterdam -- GEANT in Vienna
>
> This path primarily consists of Layer-2 Ethernet and SONET/SDH. It is
> 10GigE from aofa-sdn1 to the Ciena NYC. On the Ciena, it is mapped
> into
> a STS-1-96v (5G) circuit across the Atlantic. Once it gets to AMS, it
> is passed through the E600 and handed off to SARA as Ethernet. We
> have
> setup port mirroring on USLHCnet's E600 in AMS for the purpose of
> counting packets. VLAN tag 2607 is used all the way from ESnet to
> SARA.
> I am not sure how the SARA--GEANT portion of the circuit is handled,
> but
> I'm assuming it has been provisioned over an SDH circuit of comparable
> capacity -- e.g., VC-4-32v?
>
> Here is a traceroute between ESnet's perf tester (aofa-pt1.es.net) and
> GEANT's perf tester (ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net ):
>
> # traceroute ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net
> traceroute to ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58), 64 hops
> max, 40 byte packets
> 1 aofa-te-perf-if1 (198.124.238.41) 0.155 ms 0.102 ms 0.086 ms
> 2 esnet.rt1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.125.93) 101.117 ms 101.127 ms
> 101.371 ms
> 3 ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58) 101.163 ms
> 101.397
> ms 101.511 ms
>
> Azher and I both ran tcpdump to count packets and compared the numbers
> to the bwctl output. I am going to primarily focus on the NYC ->
> Vienna
> direction, as I have not observed any loss with 100Mbps UDP tests in
> the
> reverse direction.
>
> Here is the summary of 5 tests in the NYC -> Vienna direction, showing
> between 0.2% and 0.48% loss each time:
>
> TEST 1: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375586470 Bytes 100156068 bits/sec
> 0.021
> ms 903/256404 (0.35%)
> TEST 2: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 376156830 Bytes 100308699 bits/sec
> 0.014
> ms 506/256395 (0.2%)
> TEST 3: [ 8] 0.0-30.0 sec 375074910 Bytes 100020313 bits/sec
> 0.027
> ms 1242/256395 (0.48%)
> TEST 4: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375471810 Bytes 100125953 bits/sec
> 0.020
> ms 974/256397 (0.38%)
> TEST 5: [ 9] 0.0-30.0 sec 375468870 Bytes 100125236 bits/sec
> 0.020
> ms 974/256395 (0.38%)
>
> During these tests, Azher and I wrote packet captures to disk. The
> port
> mirroring host in AMS is using a version of libpcap < v1.0.0, so
> tcpdump
> cannot set the buffer size with -B. As a result, the first couple of
> tests were inconclusive due to pcap buffers being exhausted. Once
> Azher
> lowered the snaplen parameter to tcpdump, our packet counts started to
> match up.
>
> Here are two detailed examples. TEST 5 was over UDP port 5004. iperf
> reported 974 packets lost out of 256395 total.
>
> On the ESnet test host, we captured a total of 256455 packets going to
> ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net. Filtering out only port 5004 gives
> us
> 256398. Notice there is a difference of 3 packets. This is because
> the
> very last packet was in the reverse direction, and iperf always seems
> to
> report 2 less than reality. (see output below)
>
> -------------------------------

> # tcpdump -s 66 -ni eth3.2607 -w 2607-4.pcap host 198.124.238.42 and
> host 62.40.123.58
> tcpdump: WARNING: eth3.2607: no IPv4 address assigned
> tcpdump: listening on eth3.2607, link-type EN10MB (Ethernet), capture
> size 66 bytes
> 256457 packets captured
> 257200 packets received by filter
> 652 packets dropped by kernel
>
> # tcpdump -nr 2607-4.pcap port 5003 | wc -l
> reading from file 2607-4.pcap, link-type EN10MB (Ethernet)
> 256400
> ===
>

>
> Hello.
>
> From Joe Metzger:
> -----
> ESnet has seen a significant improvement in our test results today.
> Both
> GEANT adding additional capacity on their path and Azher adding the
> shaping
> on the Force 10 seems to have had an affect.
>
> We saw an order of magnitude drop in packet loss in UDP tests, and we
> saw a
> TCP test up in the 900Mbps range from NYC to VIE right after the
> shaping was
> deployed. Test performance seems to have dropped off a bit in the last
> couple hours,
> but we have also seen significant increases in the utilization of the
> link which
> might account for some of that effect.
>
> But at this point, I am questioning if the problem we are experiencing
> is
> some sort of fault in a piece of equipment that can be replaced once
> we
> identify it, or if there are inherent problems in the design of this
> path
> and the equipment implementing it that we didn't know about. The
> changes
> that are improving performance are pointing to an inherent equipment
> limitations.
>
> I think we should seriously consider taking this path out of service,
> and then
> rigorously testing it to see if it is capable of meeting the typical
> standards
> that ESnet has for wide area links. (IE it should be able to transfer
> 50 Terabytes
> with less than 100 packets dropped.) If it is not capable of
> performing at these
> levels, then I would like to discover what components or sections of
> the path
> are causing the problems and better characterize them so we can
> develop
> a plan
> to fix them or work around them.
>
> Does anybody object to proceeding with this plan early next week?
>
> Graph showing link utilization jump after deploying shaping:
>
>
>
https://stats1.es.net/graphite/render/?width=1110&height=580&_salt=1287174731.588&target=aofa-
> sdn1.interface.xe-0_1_0%402607.in&target=aofa-sdn1.interface.xe-
> 0_1_0%402607.out&from=08%3A00_20101015&until=16%3A00_20101015

-- by John Shade at Mon Sep 27 15:16:46 UTC 2010

Still working on troubleshooting with GARR ES-NET BNL.
Last results shows an asymmetry performances betwee CNAF and ES-NET (aofa-pt1.es.net and bnl.pt1.es.net)

CNAF(new 1Gb/s connected server)-->BNL (aofa-pt1.es.net and bnl.pt1.es.net) single Stream:  800 Mb/s
CNAF(new 1Gb/s connected server)-->newmon.bnl.gov (inside BNL campus) Single Stream:  200Mb/s
BNL (aofa-pt1.es.net or bnl.pt1.es.net) --> CNAF (new1Gb/s connected server): 20Mb/s
newmon.bnl.gov (inside BNL campus with MTU=1500) --> CNAF (new 1Gb/s connected server) Single Stream:  5Mb/s

These results are obtained using 2 different servers connected in 2 different position on the internal CNAF net (one of those directly connected to the core router).

-- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 01 11:50:23 UTC 2010

Hello.

From Chris Tracy at ESNet, (note: It will extend to the next entries due to character limit.)

-------------------------
I have just completed several tests with help from Azher Mughal in the
USLHCnet domain.

I ran 30 second, 100Mbps UDP tests with bwctl between aofa-pt1.es.net
and ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net.  Loss was seen in the NYC to
Vienna direction, but the reverse direction was clean in every test.

The path under test is:

ESnet aofa-sdn1 -- USLHCnet E600 -- Ciena NYC -- Ciena AMS -- E600AMS --
SARA.nl -- GEANT in Amsterdam -- GEANT in Vienna

This path primarily consists of Layer-2 Ethernet and SONET/SDH.  It is
10GigE from aofa-sdn1 to the Ciena NYC.  On the Ciena, it is mapped into
a STS-1-96v (5G) circuit across the Atlantic.  Once it gets to AMS, it
is passed through the E600 and handed off to SARA as Ethernet.  We have
setup port mirroring on USLHCnet's E600 in AMS for the purpose of
counting packets.  VLAN tag 2607 is used all the way from ESnet to SARA.
I am not sure how the SARA--GEANT portion of the circuit is handled, but
I'm assuming it has been provisioned over an SDH circuit of comparable
capacity -- e.g., VC-4-32v?

Here is a traceroute between ESnet's perf tester (aofa-pt1.es.net) and
GEANT's perf tester (ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net ):

# traceroute ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net
traceroute to ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58), 64 hops
max, 40 byte packets
1  aofa-te-perf-if1 (198.124.238.41)  0.155 ms  0.102 ms  0.086 ms
2  esnet.rt1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.125.93)  101.117 ms  101.127 ms
101.371 ms
3  ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net (62.40.123.58)  101.163 ms  101.397
ms  101.511 ms

Azher and I both ran tcpdump to count packets and compared the numbers
to the bwctl output.  I am going to primarily focus on the NYC -> Vienna
direction, as I have not observed any loss with 100Mbps UDP tests in the
reverse direction.

Here is the summary of 5 tests in the NYC -> Vienna direction, showing
between 0.2% and 0.48% loss each time:

TEST 1: [  8]  0.0-30.0 sec  375586470 Bytes  100156068 bits/sec  0.021
ms  903/256404 (0.35%)
TEST 2: [  8]  0.0-30.0 sec  376156830 Bytes  100308699 bits/sec  0.014
ms  506/256395 (0.2%)
TEST 3: [  8]  0.0-30.0 sec  375074910 Bytes  100020313 bits/sec  0.027
ms 1242/256395 (0.48%)
TEST 4: [  9]  0.0-30.0 sec  375471810 Bytes  100125953 bits/sec   0.020
ms  974/256397 (0.38%)
TEST 5: [  9]  0.0-30.0 sec  375468870 Bytes  100125236 bits/sec   0.020
ms  974/256395 (0.38%)

During these tests, Azher and I wrote packet captures to disk.  The port
mirroring host in AMS is using a version of libpcap < v1.0.0, so tcpdump
cannot set the buffer size with -B.  As a result, the first couple of
tests were inconclusive due to pcap buffers being exhausted.  Once Azher
lowered the snaplen parameter to tcpdump, our packet counts started to
match up.

Here are two detailed examples.  TEST 5 was over UDP port 5004.  iperf
reported 974 packets lost out of 256395 total.

On the ESnet test host, we captured a total of 256455 packets going to
ge0-vlan71.mp1.vie.at.geant2.net.  Filtering out only port 5004 gives us
256398.  Notice there is a difference of 3 packets.  This is because the
very last packet was in the reverse direction, and iperf always seems to
report 2 less than reality.  (see output below)

-------------------------------

-- by Stefano Zani at Fri Oct 08 12:10:58 UTC 2010

From my email on 10/6/10

Just a few updates about what we're going to be changing here at BNL. In the next few days we will be rerouting VLAN 315 which is our internal ATLAS network from an internal trunk to a direct etherchannel at the perimeter routers. This will make the BNL Atlas networks 2 hops closer. We also plan on increasing the available bandwidth dedicated to VLAN 315. Also, I'm in the process of setting up an additional bwctl unit to use here at BNL. I'll let you know what the IP and DNS is when I get it all setup.

More later

today 10/12/10

Also, late last week we did move the BNL internal atlas link to a more direct path. This eliminated two BNL boxes. Also I do have the new test box running. It is IP 130.199.3.80 netb10.bnl.gov. It is running bwctld so you can access it through the bwctl command. If you don't have it, I'll start up an iperf for you. The old tester 130.199.3.7 newmon.bnl.gov is also available. It to has bwctld and iperf on ports 5200 and 5201 for udp.

-- by Hironori Ito at Fri Oct 15 15:47:10 UTC 2010

Hello.

From Joe Metzger:
-----
ESnet has seen a significant improvement in our test results today. Both
GEANT adding additional capacity on their path and Azher adding the shaping
on the Force 10 seems to have had an affect.

We saw an order of magnitude drop in packet loss in UDP tests, and we saw a
TCP test up in the 900Mbps range from NYC to VIE right after the shaping was
deployed. Test performance seems to have dropped off a bit in the last couple hours,
but we have also seen significant increases in the utilization of the link which
might account for some of that effect.

But at this point, I am questioning if the problem we are experiencing is
some sort of fault in a piece of equipment that can be replaced once we
identify it, or if there are inherent problems in the design of this path
and the equipment implementing it that we didn't know about.  The changes
that are improving performance are pointing to an inherent equipment limitations.

I think we should seriously consider taking this path out of service, and then
rigorously testing it to see if it is capable of meeting the typical standards
that ESnet has for wide area links. (IE it should be able to transfer 50 Terabytes
with less than 100 packets dropped.)  If it is not capable of performing at these
levels, then I would like to discover what components or sections of the path
are causing the problems and better characterize them so we can develop a plan
to fix them or work around them.

Does anybody object to proceeding with this plan early next week?

Graph showing link utilization jump after deploying shaping:

https://stats1.es.net/graphite/render/?width=1110&height=580&_salt=1287174731.588&target=aofa-sdn1.interface.xe-0_1_0%402607.in&target=aofa-sdn1.interface.xe-0_1_0%402607.out&from=08%3A00_20101015&until=16%3A00_20101015

------

Due to the actions taken by the NRENs (in GEANT domain)   the performance have been improved and the transfers between BNL and CNAF are not failing any more.
We are still measuring an asymmetry in pure network performache (memory to memory transfers) between CNAF and BNL but at  higher rates than before (one order of magnitude).
From a network point of view we will continue to follow up the remaining troubleshooting activity with NRENs but we suggest to close this ticket.
